My dentist enthusiastically recommend this device, and claimed that there are studies who claim that use of this device is as good or better than conventional brushing and flossing. After spending so much $ on reparative work, for this price, let me try it out.  I am desperate.  OK, not perfect.  Use once for 5 minutes per 2 hours.  Sprays about.  Still learning how to use it.  How will it hold up over time?  How well will I keep the reservoir and device clean?  For now, it seems to work well.  It seems to clean well.  I warm up water for reservoir in a microwave container in a microwave oven.  My initial impression: If it holds up, until someone engineers a better / stronger device, it seems to do what it is expected to do, and I perceive that this a better than what I had been using for my dental hygiene.  And the cost of the device is IMO quite reasonable (w 3Y warranty).</li>

    <li> I have a bias against this tool, because it is a baldface ripoff of my grandfather&#x27;s invention of the oral irrigator.  Dr. C.D. Matteson conceived, invented, patented and produced by hand the original prototype in 1953 in Ft Collins, CO.  When I lived as a child in Arlington, VA, he came to visit and spent most of the visit getting the patent done.  In 1955-56, when I lived in Ft Collins, my brother and I demonstrated the oral irrigator for his colleagues.  On of his &amp;#34;friends&amp;#34; was Mr. Mattingly.  He was impressed with it and wanted to partner up with my grandfather to manufacture it.  That did not go well.  My grandfather&#x27;s invention was directly screwed on the faucet, had no motor of any type nor electricity and provided a continuous 90 lbs of pressure flow.  The valve had the ability to direct the flow to the syringe or directly from the faucet by use of a turnable knob.  Mattingly did some work arounds to add a motorized pump and a pulsating flow, neither of which is desirable.  So, by purchasing this fraud, I feel as though I am a traitor to my grandfather&#x27;s vision, but my valve that he invented does not fit on my faucet, so I purchased this instead.  It is better than nothing.</li>

    <li> ASTONISHING (to me, anyway) HEALTH UPDATE (2/19/2017): WATERPIKING SAVES LIVES, MAYBE YOURS! REALLY! I MEAN IT! (I know, it sounds crazy...)&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I finally broke down and got a Waterpik when my dentist told me I had periodontal pockets and would need a deep cleaning. I read somewhere that with regular use of a Waterpik, I might just be able to reverse those pockets and eliminate that need for an uncomfortable deep cleaning. I gave it a three-month try and it worked! No deep cleaning needed!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Also, I spoke with my primary care physician about plaque, and learned that there are two more (one of them could save your life) benefits to Waterpiking regularly. See my UPDATE at the end of this review.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I have noticed that others have asked a lot of the questions that I had early on inside of their reviews and in the customer questions section. So I thought I would gather up all of the answers and put them in one review. I hope this will be your Guide to Using Your New Aquarius Waterpik.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;If you do find this review helpful, please click &amp;#34;Yes&amp;#34; below, I&#x27;d appreciate it!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;HOW DO I AVOID MAKING MY GUMS BLEED WHEN I START USING MY WATERPIK?&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;It is not in the instructions anymore, but according to my husband, Waterpik used always to tell users to start by using the lowest &amp;#34;1&amp;#34; pressure setting and then to turn the pressure up one notch per day to get your gums adjusted to the Waterpik&#x27;s pressure gradually. If you do this, you should be on &amp;#34;10&amp;#34;, or whatever setting you prefer, in no time and with no gum bleeding.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;HOW DO I KEEP FROM SPLASHING WATER EVERYWHERE?&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;There are two simple tricks never to see a water splash again. First, don&#x27;t turn the Waterpik on until it is in your mouth. Second, keep your mouth closed except a slight parting of your lips to allow water to drain out of your mouth, while you use your Waterpik. That should take care of it!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;THE ON/OFF SWITCH ON THE HANDLE IS HARD TO USE.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;You will, unfortunately, just have to get the hang of how to master that switch. It seems to be a matter to where you apply pressure on the switch. It seems to work best when you apply pressure close to the center, rather than from the bottom or the top, in my limited experience. However, in the meantime, if you get frustrated, just use the on/off button on the face of the machine as a shortcut.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;WHY DO THEY SEND SEVEN TIPS BUT ONLY PROVIDE SLOTS FOR TWO?&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;First of all, you only receive four different types of tips. The total number of tips adds up to seven because Waterpik provides three identical Classic Jet Tips (see below for descriptions of each). Most people choose only one style of tip for daily use (possibly two if you have periodontal pockets). The second slot can also be used for a partner or house-guest.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;WHAT IS THE DIFFERENCE BETWEEN THE FOUR STYLES OF TIPS INCLUDED?&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&amp;#34;CLASSIC JET TIP&amp;#34; (you get 3)&lt;br /&gt;To identify it: it is the only tip style that you get three of.&lt;br /&gt;Classic Jet Tips are for general use and replace flossing for people without crowns or other more-serious-than-fillings dental work. (For people with that sort of dental work, use the &amp;#34;Plaque Seeker Tip&amp;#34;, described below.) Use the Classic Jet Tip unless you have a special reason to choose one of the others.&lt;br /&gt;Rather than include links to the replacement tips in this review, I recommend that you just do a search for &amp;#34;Waterpik JT-100E&amp;#34;. That way, there&#x27;s no risk that this review will be filled with dead links.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;If you search by the tip&#x27;s name, you will probably get results that include tips that are not compatible with your Aquarius. So I have provided the actual model numbers of each tip so that you can search for the right one. If any tip that you want is not available on Amazon, you can buy it directly from Waterpik dot com. (Note For Ultra Buyers: the Ultra uses the same modeltips as the Aquarius, provided here.)&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&amp;#34;TOOTHBRUSH TIP&amp;#34; (quantity: 1, but that is plenty for most)&lt;br /&gt;To identify it: it looks like a tiny toothbrush.&lt;br /&gt;This tip allows you to brush your teeth and Waterpik at the same time. As efficient as that sounds, there must be a reason why they included 3 Classic Jet Tips and only 1 Toothbrush Tip. I am guessing the reason is that this Brush Tip looks more efficient than it is -- especially if you have an effective toothbrush like a Sonicare.&lt;br /&gt;Search for &amp;#34;Waterpik TB-100E&amp;#34; to find compatible replacement tips.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&amp;#34;PLAQUE SEEKER TIP&amp;#34; (quantity: 1) (my daily use tip)&lt;br /&gt;To identify it: look for fewer bristles than are on the Toothbrush Tip.&lt;br /&gt;The Plaque Seeker Tip is designed for use with crown, implants, and bridges, as well as for general use. So if you have any dental work more serious than fillings in your mouth (i.e. are you over 30?), you can just use this tip as your daily tip all around your mouth. &amp;#34;Removes bacteria and debris from hard to reach areas around dental restorations.&amp;#34;&lt;br /&gt;Search for &amp;#34;Waterpik PS-100E&amp;#34; to buy refills.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&amp;#34;PIK POCKET TIP&amp;#34; (quantity: 1)&lt;br /&gt;To identify it: it looks like the Classic Jet Tip but with an extra pointy attachment at the end.&lt;br /&gt;This one is for people who have periodontal pockets or furcations. It can &amp;#34;deliver medicaments&amp;#34; except that neither the Aquarius nor the Ultra is designed for that (they don&#x27;t have &amp;#34;Medicament Reservoirs&amp;#34;), or just rinse deep below the gumline. Few people will choose to use the Pik Pocket as their daily tip. You would use this before or after you do your primary Waterpik rinse, and probably just on the areas that need it. This tip is supposed to be used only with the machine set to a pressure of &amp;#34;1&amp;#34;, so don&#x27;t forget to turn the pressure down before using it.&lt;br /&gt;Search for &amp;#34;PP-100E&amp;#34; to get compatible replacement tips.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;OTHER WATERPIK TIPS YOU CAN BUY ON AMAZON COMPATIBLE WITH THE WATERPIK AQUARIUS: these don&#x27;t come with your Aquarius but they are compatible with it, and you may find them useful:&lt;br /&gt;--Orthodontic tip OD-100E&lt;br /&gt;--Tongue Cleaner TC-100E&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Finally, Waterpik also offers a storage case that comes with six compatible tips. Search for TS-100E.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;THE WATERPIK AQUARIUS VERUS THE WATERPIK ULTRA: A SHOWDOWN&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Some reviewers have argued that the older [[ASIN:B00CU9VF2Q Waterpik WP100W Ultra Dental Water Flosser]] is a better device. However, many reviewers have claimed the opposite. Waterpik continues to make both. Here are the differences according to Amazon and Waterpik (you can do comparisons between any current models on Waterpik&#x27;s website, just type in Waterpik dot com then choose Oral Hygiene):&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This Model, the Waterpik Aquarius WP-660 is called the &amp;#34;Aquarius Professional&amp;#34; on Waterpik&#x27;s site. That&#x27;s cool, right?&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;As of this writing, the Ultra has fewer than 300 reviews that average 4.5 stars; this Aquarius has over 6,000 reviews that average 4.4 stars. Since I don&#x27;t know if the Ultra&#x27;s average rating is 4.500000 and the Aquarius&#x27;s is 4.4999999999, I don&#x27;t really see any difference in those reviews other than than a LOT more people choose to buy this Aquarius.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Differences Between this Aquarius and the [[ASIN:B00CU9VF2Q Ultra]]&lt;br /&gt;--while on Amazon, prices vary, Waterpik thinks the Aquarius is the nicer machine because they charge $20 more for the Aquarius than for the Ultra;&lt;br /&gt;--the Ultra has a button on the handle that you must hold down in order to keep the water flowing, if you let go, it stops; the Aquarius has an on/off toggle switch so that once you toggle it on, it keeps flowing without finger pressure, until you toggle it off;&lt;br /&gt;--the Aquarius comes with three Classic Jet tips, versus two with the Ultra&lt;br /&gt;--the Aquarius includes a massage mode (have to admit that I don&#x27;t use this at all)&lt;br/&gt;--the Aquarius includes an LED Function Indicator (ehh)&lt;br /&gt;--the Aquarius includes a Timer/Pacer (I use this every day and know that I would stop sooner than I should if it weren&#x27;t on there)&lt;br /&gt;--the Ultra doesn&#x27;t include anything that the Aquarius does not&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Features That Are Identical Between the Aquarius and the Ultra&lt;br /&gt;--both come in black and white (Aquarius, this page; [[ASIN:B00CU9VF2Q Waterpik Ultra White and Black available here]];&lt;br /&gt;--same water pressure&lt;br /&gt;--same flow rate&lt;br /&gt;--same pulse rate&lt;br /&gt;--both have 10 pressure settings&lt;br /&gt;--the tips rotate 360 degrees&lt;br /&gt;--water capacity both in volume and in seconds&lt;br /&gt;--both have covered water reservoirs&lt;br /&gt;--almost identical weight: 1.46 pounds for this Aquarius and 1.48 for the Ultra&lt;br /&gt;--both have three-year warranties&lt;br /&gt;--both only have plugs for North America&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;SOME OTHER MODELS AVAILABLE:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Waterpik Complete Care is still available for $10 more and gives you a shorter warranty (2 years instead of 3), no massage mode, no LED indicators, and fewer tips.     <li> I like this unit very much, but at first I gave it only four stars because of one problem that I thought must be a small design flaw. On this unit there is an on/off switch on the handle, as well as a power button on the base. The instructions say to turn on the power button, then when you have the tip in your mouth to turn on the switch on the handle, and turn the handle switch off when finished. HOWEVER, I found it almost impossible to turn the water switch on and off without using two thumbs. I simply could not do it while it was in my mouth, even after I had used for nearly a month. When I called the company I was told just to work the switch back and forth several times for a few days, but this did not work So, I resorted to simply turning the power button on and off, and ignoring the on/off switch on the handle. This seems to work fine (and I found myself wondering why they even had a switch on the handle) .BUT I also went to the company website and recorded my comments there. I was pleasantly surprised to receive a phone call from a company representative just a few days later, telling me that this was unusual and that they would immediately sent me a replacement handle. It came in just a few days, and it worked beautifully! So I am really pleased with this company. the flosser works very well. I use it after I have brushed and flossed with regular floss, and nearly always I will dislodge at least a little more of something that was not dislodged before.I had a portable water flosser that I bought back in 2007, but it finally wore out, so I decided to replace it with this one.I am glad I did. If you buy one and have a problem similar to the one I described, don&#x27;t hesitate to notify the company (through their website worked better for me than by telephone).&lt;br /&gt;One thing I do not understand is why the company recommends replacing the tips every 6 months.     <li> I was skeptical at first, but after having this for a few years now I&#x27;m glad I tried it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;PROS:&lt;br /&gt;â€¢ Easy to Use - Fill it with warm water or water mixed with mouthwash (same amount of mouthwash you&#x27;d normally use diluted in the water), choose the intensity and your head attachment, put the wand end in your mouth, make sure the switch on the wand is turned on (I leave mine turned on), turn the power button on, start at a back molar and work your way forward, keeping your head tilted forward and lips puckered so the water pours out into the sink.&lt;br /&gt;â€¢ Efficacy - More effective and faster than flossing. At least that&#x27;s what the internet says, but here&#x27;s my point: I never would floss, but this is so easy and quick I can do it every night with no worry. It also leaves your mouth feeling refreshed and rinsed before you brush and mouthwash.&lt;br /&gt;â€¢ Oral Hygiene - The water pushes bacteria and food particles out, effectively doing the same job as flossing and mouthwashing. It also helps promote periodontal health by stimulating circulation in your gums, which can help them to heal faster and fight infections better.&lt;br /&gt;â€¢ No pain or bleeding if you just start, unlike flossing. Just start on the lowest sensitivity and work your way up.&lt;br /&gt;â€¢ Multiple Options - With various heads so you can actually brush your teeth with it, use different spray types, and the pulsating massage mode for massaging gums.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;CONS:&lt;br /&gt;â€¢ Expensive, especially compared to floss.&lt;br /&gt;â€¢ The on/off switch is difficult to change with one hand. This doesn&#x27;t affect me though as I leave it on and just use the power button on the machine to start and stop water flow.&lt;br /&gt;â€¢ Can be loud, if you&#x27;re trying to floss while others are asleep.&lt;br /&gt;â€¢ Not portable like floss is. Even if you get the handheld version (terrible idea) you have to dispose of the water, so you can&#x27;t floss while you read or watch TV like with standard floss.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;TIPS:&lt;br /&gt;â€¢ Putting a washcloth or grip pad (like what you line cabinets with or what you open the pickle jar with) under the unit to help lower the vibrations&lt;br /&gt;â€¢ Once a month do a cleaning rinse: Clean the basin out with vinegar, allowing it to soak for an hour and put the wand tips in with it - this will kill odor causing germs. Pour that out and do a full hot water rinse to get the vinegar out, then do a hydrogen peroxide rinse. The peroxide will kill any mildew spores inside the tubing.&lt;br /&gt;â€¢ Don&#x27;t leave water in the basin, or put any non-liquid or sticky additives in. I&#x27;ve put mouthwash in before as a rinse aid, but that&#x27;s it. You don&#x27;t want stuff clogging the tubing.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;UPDATE: After over two years it&#x27;s still performing like new, staying clean inside and out, and my teeth have never been healthier! I&#x27;ve also not seen any signs of leaking like others have experienced. The only time I get water on the counter is if it runs along the hose and drips off.d (like what you line cabinets with or what you open the pickle jar with) under the unit to help lower the vibrations&lt;br /&gt;â€¢ Once a month do a cleaning rinse: Clean the basin out with vinegar, allowing it to soak for an hour and put the wand tips in with it - this will kill odor causing germs.     <li> I&#x27;m not a dentist or dental hygienist , or even a (fluid mechanics, perhaps) physicist, so I can&#x27;t tell you whether the Waterpik WP-660 \\&quot;Professional\\&quot; Water Flosser is better than a thorough brushing followed by brushing.  However, if your dental professional recommends a WaterPik, I *can* report that I&#x27;m very happy with this model, although some of the various tips seem a little superfluous.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Unlike some reviewers here, I&#x27;ve had no problems with the truly convenient on/off switch located on the handle; the switch enables you to turn the machine on while the device is in your mouth, preventing the extra-oral spraying all over your bathroom.  Good job there!  Nor have I had any problem seating the waterpik back in its holder, or noticed any mold forming.  (They recommend cleaning with vinegar solution, oh, and YES, you can use this with mouth wash-just rinse the device afterwards.)&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;A few highlights include:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;1. A nice continuous (it does not adjust at \\&quot;click points\\&quot;) power dial, and the very real difference in these power settings.  Depending on preferences and the health of your gums, you can very easily adjust from a very light stream to one so powerful it may hurt in certain areas.  You can even change the jet stream power while using it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;2. Adequate water supply.  The built-in tank (it&#x27;s well held in place by a thin plastic cover) holds enough water to do a thorough cleaning of all your teeth and gums.  If you sometimes want a little extra gum massage/cleaning, it&#x27;s very fast and easy to just fill up the small, light plastic tank again.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;3. Smaller footprint, semi-stylish design.  This will take up less room on a counter top (check the dimensions given by Amazon above) than Waterpiks from the past, and it&#x27;s not nearly as unwieldy looking.  While hard white plastic with an attached cleaning device sticking up (see pictures) isn&#x27;t going to enhance your bathroom&#x27;s appearance, the look is a definite improvement compared to some of the clunkers I had several years ago.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;4. Overall quality.  Although I&#x27;ve used this for only a couple of months, I&#x27;m impressed with the overall functioning of the Waterpik.  It&#x27;s been reliable, it has a strong motor, the timer feature (so that you can pace your cleaning) works every time, and the power is impressive.  There&#x27;s a massage feature that give you a pulse rather than a continuous flow. I didn&#x27;t see the need for this at first, but I now prefer it when my purpose is to massage the gums only.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;5.It&#x27;s a bit noisy, but not more than I expected. However, if your bathroom (or wherever the heck you use this) is close to a bedroom where your partner sleeps, you&#x27;ll want to close all doors.  It might even be better to Waterpik when he or she is awake.  The dog seems neutral.  The tips that are placed into the handle are locked with a small twist of a circular ring.  Very easy to do, but there is a bit of vibration to the top that is mildly annoying. I say \\&quot;mildly\\&quot; because it does not seem to affect performance; on the other hand, my irritation comes from a sense that it should have a tighter fit. Just an engineering aesthetic preference, not something that should keep you from buying this.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Those Bells and Whistles...  Timers, LED light displays, a closed compartment for two extra tips, and five types of tips, I wonder if they really make much of a difference, especially the tips (the timer and LED work fine and seem pretty standard on dental appliances these days).  The tips though...  You get a thin hard tip to deliver water \\&quot;deep into periodontal pockets,\\&quot;  a flat one to clean your tongue, a sort of soft tiny brush tip  to brush teeth \\&quot;and all around [the] orthodontic bracket, \\&quot; a toothbrush tip (standard looking circular brush), and the bristled \\&quot;plaque-seeker\\&quot; tip (\\&quot;Gently brush along the gumline, pausing briefly between teeth to gently brush and allow the water to flow between  the teeth.\\&quot;)  [Quotes from the very thorough and easy-to-understand included manual.]&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Some of these seem not entirely effective to me. For example, using the brush with toothpaste doesn&#x27;t work that well , because the water stream volume quickly gets rid of the tooth paste. (However, the manual does state it can be used with or without paste).  The e plaque-seeker&#x27;s brush just doesn&#x27;t seem much better than the general use \\&quot;classic jet tip,\\&quot; but perhaps others will find it helpful. So far, I haven&#x27;t.  Not a big complaint, but I imagine it may add a little to the cost.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Summary.  I&#x27;m very satisfied with this new Waterpik and enjoy using it.  My mouth *feels* extra clean afteruse.  Is it cleaner than doing a thorough flossing...I don&#x27;t know.  However, you might consider whether you&#x27;ll take better care of your teeth with a well-working gadget that is easy to use and leaves a subjective feeling of CLEAN TEETH.  The gumline massage capability seems superior to flossing.  If you&#x27;re not a skeptic, consider the company&#x27;s claim that \\&quot;Flossers are clinically proven to remove up to 99.9% of plaque from treated areas in 3 seconds. And for healthier gums, they are clinically proven up to 50% more effective for improving gum health vs. string floss.\\&quot;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I&#x27;d like to see the price about $10 lower than the current non-discounted price, so it&#x27;s not great, but reasonably good value.  If it motivates you to clean you teeth and gums more often than before, it&#x27;s an excellent value!  : )  As always, consult your oral hygiene specialist to see whether the Waterpik is a wise choice for you.orough and easy-to-understand included manual.]&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Some of these seem not entirely effective to me.     <li> For about a year now, I&#x27;ve used the Waterpik Ultra Water Flosser and loved the unit.  It got my teeth clean, was simple to use, and made dentist visits much more bearable knowing I didn&#x27;t huge pockets in my gums anymore.  Recently I got the opportunity to try out the Waterpik Aquarius Water Flosser.  The upgrades to the unit, while few, are quite nice to have.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;First off, the huge cover that stored all the Waterpik pieces is finally gone.  I hated having all the pieces in the lid of the Ultra Water Flosser.  In the Aquarius, you can store your two favorite pieces in a space between the reservoir and the plastic side.  All the additional pieces I placed in a drawer.  This helped make the unit much more visually appealing and I no longer have to worry about pieces falling out of the lid every time I open the reservoir.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Another update is that there is a pulse that helps time you so you move from places to place in your mouth.  The water pulse goes off at the 30 and 60 second time.  This pulse didn&#x27;t really help much for me as I tend to move the pik through my mouth slowly anyways.  It was interesting to use the new &amp;#34;massage&amp;#34; feature where the water pulses continually.  The pulsing may be more appealing to others, as I didn&#x27;t find it very useful.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The final upgrade on the Aquarius unit is the &amp;#34;on/off&amp;#34; switch on the handle of the Waterpik.  This was another great addition to the pik.  On the Ultra Water you would have to push and hold down a button to keep water from squirting all over the place. I have a PhD in engineering and have designed many health and medical products, so I should be able to figure out how to turn on a waterpik.  This one simply does not work.  I checked everything including the voltage on the AC line.&lt;br /&gt;SUMMARY:&lt;br /&gt;The product sold to me was previously used but sold AS NEW, it was defective, it was unsanitary, just plain disgusting.&lt;br /&gt;So, in my assessment, the product was defective, then it was probably returned for that reason, repackaged by some thoughtless idiot, and resold as new.&lt;br /&gt;I will not return the product, I&#x27;ll keep it for show and tell.  In my profession and for my many students, it will be an excellent example of everything that could possibly go wrong with the marketing and sale of a health/medical product.  For that purpose it is worth the $60.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;NOTE: in 15 years of on-line shopping, this is only the second negative review I have ever written.  I hope it has a positive effect.</li>

    <li> UPDATE JUNE &#x27;17 I&#x27;m sorry to say that my review below may no longer be valid. I recenly saw and handled a Waterpik Ultra at Costco, and while it still has the same model number and general appearance of an Ultra, the build quality and weight felt much cheaper and toy-like compared to the older model I have at home. So I defintiely can&#x27;t claim that the Ultra I handled is any better--and who knows, it might actually be worse--when compared to the Aquarius. Very disappointing for Waterpik to keep the name and model number, while changing the build quality. So in the toss-up between Aquarius and Ultra now, I&#x27;d go with whichever one was cheaper, and if prices are similar, I pick the Aquarius for its better appearance.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;UPDATE OCT &#x27;14: The Aquarius has dropped significantly in price since my original review, and is actually slightly cheaper now than the older Ultra. So, with prices so comparable, which unit should you buy? Unless you&#x27;re really in love with the updated look of the Aquarius, the Ultra still remains the better choice for the reasons I mention below. Also take a look at the video in the &amp;#34;Most Helpful Favorable Review,&amp;#34; where you can really see the cheap construction of the Aquarius, and how sloppily the hose holsters into the unit compared to the Ultra. This sort of negates its one advantage--the cleaner-looking design--and you&#x27;ll be wrangling to holster that hose on a daily basis. No thanks!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;ORIGINAL REVIEW: Let me not waste your time and cut right to the chase: if you&#x27;re thinking about buying your first Waterpik flosser--or wondering if it&#x27;s time to upgrade your Ultra model--there&#x27;s only one reason to consider the pricey WP-660 Aquarius: it looks nicer and more modern than the now dated design of the Ultra. So if appearance isn&#x27;t important to you, stop reading right here and just go buy the cheaper Ultra, which (as I&#x27;ll get to in a moment) is better in just about every other way.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;As it so happens, an attractive, modern design IS important to me, especially in an appliance that I&#x27;m going to look at all the time in my bathroom. But even in this regard I&#x27;d say the Aquarius is good but not great. It is definitely NOT an improvement in design that will have you looking past its ergonomic flaws vs. the Ultra.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;First, the on/off water flow switch is less user friendly in operation than the on/off button on the Ultra. Admittedly, there were issues with button failure at one time on the Ultra, but the replacement handle I received from Waterpik has been working for over a year now with no problems, so this seems to have been resolved.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Second, getting the handle and hose &amp;#34;re-holstered&amp;#34; on the Aquarius is more finicky than it is on the Ultra--plus the hose never seems to sit in the unit as neatly.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Third, the Aquarius weighs A FULL POUND less than the 2.5 pound Ultra, and you can&#x27;t help but think that the weight was trimmed by using a lighter and less durable pump mechanism. Time will tell if that&#x27;s really the case, but I&#x27;ve also found that the lightness of the Aquarius causes it to shift around too easily on my bathroom counter.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Fourth, only two tips can be stored in the unit vs. all the tips being storable in the Ultra&#x27;s lid. Waterpik has probably learned that its customers are fine with more limited tip storage, but again, this is no step forward.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Fifth, the dual modes on the Aquarius--which could be seen as its only real advance vs. the single mode Ultra--are just a marketing gimmick. If you just want to massage your gums with the Ultra, simply dial down the water flow pressure and massage away. There&#x27;s no need for a special mode to do this.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Bottom line: water flossing is a mature technology, and there are few if any &amp;#34;functional&amp;#34; reasons to introduce a new model. So it&#x27;s a shame that Waterpik didn&#x27;t make more of an effort to at least achieve better ergonomics in a killer new design with the Aquarius. You can pay 20%+ more than the Ultra and get the somewhat nicer looking but ergonomically inferior Aquarius. Or you can just buy the Ultra and not bother to upgrade if you already own it. Both units will give you the same 5-star flossing ability. The Ultra will let you hang onto some extra cash while doing it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Thanks for taking the time to read my review and I hope you find it helpful in making a buying decision!n pay 20%+ more than the Ultra and get the somewhat nicer looking but ergonomically inferior Aquarius. Or you can just buy the Ultra and not bother to upgrade if you already own it. Both units will give you the same 5-star flossing ability. The Ultra will let you hang onto some extra cash while doing it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Thanks for taking the time to read my review and I hope you find it helpful in making a buying decision!</li>

    <li> I have an older Waterpik that is approximately 5 years old. It&#x27;s done a good job but from the first time I used it, I felt like it was a little rough around the edges and very noisy. This new model is a considerable step up from that earlier one.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;For example, the handle has a spray-stop function. On the old one, it was a &amp;#34;press and hold&amp;#34; type of button and even when pressing your hardest, it still dribbled water and made a mess. The new one has a switch, and when it&#x27;s switched off, the water is stopped completely. Very handy when you need to make an adjustment and don&#x27;t need to turn it off entirely.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;It also includes a massage mode that would be good for those with gum problems by cycling from &amp;#34;floss&amp;#34; to &amp;#34;massage&amp;#34; with the button on the body.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;But most of all, the motor is much quieter, less an obnoxious grind and more of an aggressive purr. I&#x27;m not sure what has changed about how it uses water, but I am able to make it through my entire mouth and take my time where the old unit would have me rushing through to finish. Appears to be about the same amount of water, and they both do an equally good job, so the new model must be more efficient in some way.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;One minor downside to the new unit is nozzle storage. On the old one, it was a clamshell cover for the water cup that could contain a handful of different spray nozzles.     <li> [[VIDEOID:mo1GFD1DUOD3AR7]]When my dentist made me a bridge, she recommended to me to get a dental water jet system for cleaning - a Waterpik.  Ordinary floss will no longer do the job as it cannot squeeze in between my new teeth.  Not very familiar at that time about what a Waterpik is, I went to do my research and bought Waterpik Ultra Water Flosser.  That was 3 years ago, now I have this new Waterpik Aquarius model.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;It occupies a small footprint.  The jet has 10 power settings just like the older model.  For my preference, I think 1 to 3 is weak, while 8 to 10 is too strong, so I stay right in the middle.  I recommend to start by using the number 3 setting and adjust the knob as it suits you.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;There are a number of differences from the older model.&lt;br /&gt;a) The Aquarius is more compact (although sacrificing a space for the accessories that used to be on the lid of the water reservoir - now you would need to find a place for the other tips. I put mine in the medicine cabinet). There is still a place for two extra tips; it is now located directly inside the water tank.&lt;br /&gt;b) The addition of the gum massage button and LED.&lt;br /&gt;c) Neutral colors provides better aesthetics.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Water tank:&lt;br /&gt;I filled the older water tank with water and then pour it to the water tank of the new Aquarius.  It may look that the older model has more capacity but I found out they are just the same.  The new tank has a smaller footprint but is taller.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cons:&lt;br /&gt;- as with the older model, the water comes out of the tip if you forget to place it back on the hook.  This sometimes happen with the kids and have a pool of water by the side of the sink or on the floor.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;What is missing?&lt;br /&gt;- an ultrasonic vibration action that is present on my Interplak water dental jet system&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;There are multiple attachments included.     <li> I&#x27;m an adult with braces (recently hit my 2 year mark) and have been using a Waterpik WP-100 a.k.a the Waterpik Ultra water flosser for the entire time I&#x27;ve had my braces. Like many folks who wear braces I found that using traditional cleansing techniques was both extremely time consuming and still left food particles in my braces. The Waterpik came recommended by my dentist and orthodontist. So I jumped at the opportunity to try the WP-660.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;--------------------&lt;br /&gt;DESIGN:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The WP-660 is very similar to my WP-100. Both feature a water reservoir, hose connected wand attachment with interchangeable cleaning heads. The major changes between the two seem to be color; the WP-660 is entirely white with a clear reservoir. The wand itself on the 660 has a toggle for controlling the water stream instead of a button that required depressing on my WP-100. The WP-660 also features a massaging feature (controlled on the main body instead of the wand) not present on the WP-100.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Strangely the 660 is missing the tool compartment for storing all the different cleaning attachments that my WP-100 has. This was a compartment dome that fit inside the lid of the reservoir. Additionally there is not included storage case of any type. Meaning that if you switch between cleaning heads you&#x27;re going to have to store your attachments somewhere of your own choosing or purchase a storage case.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The WP-660 despite being a more expensive than my older 100-series also feels a bit more cheaply constructed. The plastics, particularly on the reservoir and lid feel cheaper and less durable.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;--------------------&lt;br /&gt;USE:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Functionally both the 660 and 100-series are very similar. I use the orthodontic-tip attachment most because of my braces and can easily withstand the stream from the WP-100 even at it&#x27;s highest setting (10). That is not the case with the 660 and the water stream feels considerably stronger. In fact the manual for the 660 specifically points out not to use the highest water pressure setting for cleaning teeth. The massage feature is the other major change in the 660 and actually find it quite nice after thoroughly cleaning my teeth with the orthodontic-tip attachment. The massage feature essentially pulses water and helps promote gum health.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Both the 660 and the 100 are loud but in different ways. I found the pitch of the WP-100 sounded more high-pitched, almost like a whine; and in the 660 it sounds lower, almost like a engine. Bottom-line is that neither is a quiet device though I found that I quickly adjusted to hearing it while cleaning my teeth in the same way that I adjusted to hearing my electric toothbrush.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Similarly both devices are about the same size. Each takes up considerable real-estate on my bathroom counter but has become an indispensable part of my hygiene routine that it&#x27;s worth the small inconvenience.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;--------------------&lt;br /&gt;WHAT I LIKE:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;(+) The same cleaning action of my older WP-100 \\&quot;Ultra\\&quot; model with a little extra power and increased water pressure.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;(+) For a person with braces having a Waterpik is a must. This little device along with brushing and flossing will leave your mouth feeling clean. It&#x27;s also perfect for quick rinses after eating foods when you don&#x27;t have time for a full cleaning.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;(+) Neat, clean aesthetics. The device looks good, stores easily and is easy to clean.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;--------------------&lt;br /&gt;WHAT I DON&#x27;T LIKE:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;(-) The WP-660 is, like its predecessor, extremely loud.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;(-) No included on-board storage for attachments.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;(-) Cheaper feeling plastics compared to the WP-100. Hopefully the cost savings that Waterpik implemented doesn&#x27;t carry over to the internal components of 660.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;(-) Besides the massage feature and increased water pressure there&#x27;s little reason to purchase the WP-660 over the WP-100.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;--------------------&lt;br/&gt;CONCLUSION:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The WP-660 is a decent, well-featured water flosser. However, compared to the cheaper WP-100 Ultra there&#x27;s little reason to spend the extra money. Recommended, but also check out the WP-100 to see if that fits your needs first!/&gt;CONCLUSION:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The WP-660 is a decent, well-featured water flosser. However, compared to the cheaper WP-100 Ultra there&#x27;s little reason to spend the extra money. Recommended, but also check out the WP-100 to see if that fits your needs first!</li>

I disagree with the term &amp;#34;water flosser.&amp;#34;  It&#x27;s a water pik and does not floss.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This is a nice unit with a 3-year warranty.  The reservoir comes out easily and it grabs whatever is necessary when putting back on.  No pushing it down to make it grab.  Put it back, turn it on, and out comes the water.  I like that the lid is not part of the reservoir.  My last garbage water pik, I dropped the reservoir and the lid cracked off.  The lid is part of the machine, so you cover it when you&#x27;re using the unit and obviously when it&#x27;s resting.  And there are holes in the lid so that it seems to air out and no thought of getting maybe moldy.  I shake the reservoir &amp;#34;dry&amp;#34; before putting it back and the holes in the lid seem to keep it &amp;#34;clean&amp;#34; or something like that.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I&#x27;m using the unit at 8.  The highest is 10.  I use 10 when I fill the unit halfway with water and &amp;#34;clean it out&amp;#34; to expunge the baking soda that I&#x27;ve added.  But in my mouth, I stick with 8.  It&#x27;s strong enough.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I don&#x27;t care about the on/off switch on the handle.  I put the thing in my mouth and then turn the unit on.  I also don&#x27;t care about the 30 second markers.  I use the entire reservoir going tooth to tooth first in the front and then in the back.  I like that 30-second thing on the Sonicare so I&#x27;m sure to give each quadrant 30 seconds of brushing but don&#x27;t see the benefit of that in the water pik.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Hoping to get at least 3 years of service from this unit.  I will check in in a year to report back!</li>

    <li> It&#x27;s been probably ten years or more since I&#x27;ve owned a water flosser; my last one was for when I had braces as a kid.     <li> my dentist says it works</li>
    <li> Looking at the reviews, there seems to be a consistent effort by what I take are some owners of the venerable Waterpik WP-100 Ultra to trash this new model and portrait it as inferior to the WP-100. I don&#x27;t think this is the case, the WP-660 is an improvement over the WP-100 in many ways and I&#x27;ll tell you why later. The funny thing is that when I bought my WP-100 about six years ago, there were some reviews from what I take were owners of the revered WP-60 Classic trashing the WP-100. I take some people prefer the old to the new and that&#x27;s OK. But I think some reviewers are being unfair to the Aquarius&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I owned a WP-100 that lasted for little over six years, used almost every day by two people, those are a lot of days so the WP-100 is an outstanding product. I did have to replace the water reservoir once due to the cheap rubber valve mechanism -improved on the Aquarius as you will see- that failed after three years of use and started leaking. Also, the hook for the handle broke -also improved on the Aquarius- and it was very difficult if not impossible to hang the handle onto the Waterpik body, I had to makeshift a Velcro handle that looked terrible. Googleing around I was surprised to find that this is a common issue with the WP-100, some owners have replaced the entire unit just because of a broken handle as there is no spare part available from Waterpik. Boomer&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;But other than those two issues, my Ultra worked flawlessly, I never had to replace the hose or the handle as some owners had to, the on-off switch never failed and it worked the same way it was when new until an accident damaged the power-cord and it stopped working. Given its state with the handle hook and its age, I thought about self-repairing it but then I decided it was time for a new unit. At first and reading all those pro-WP-100 anti-WP-660 reviews I was tempted to get another WP-100, but the price of the Aquarius was about the same as the Ultra so I decided to give it a try&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I&#x27;m glad I did. The first thing you notice with the Aquarius is its modern look and high quality materials, all white and clear, and gorgeous, a significant design improvement over the WP-100. It is also lighter, which some can argue is a good thing -like me- and some can argue it is a bad thing because it \\&quot;feels\\&quot; cheap, which is also a valid point. The important thing is that its weight doesn&#x27;t compromise its operation in any way, it won&#x27;t tip-off when used nor will slide or be unstable, it is just lighter. It might be due to the use of cheaper materials on the pump as some have argued here, or just lighter materials, an overall technological improvement rather than cheapening the unit off. I guess time will tell which one is more durable, or we will have to open both units and compare its guts to get a final answer. So, why is the Aquarius better than the WP-100, other than it looks?&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;-The WP-660 is less noisy and runs smother than the WP-100, you notice this right away. This with no compromise to the water pressure, the pressure is steady, as or more powerful than the WP-100 but it runs better, it sounds less stressed. Same or better results with less noise.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;-The hook for the handle was replaced by a sturdier piece and a different design to hold the handle, which reduces the pressure on the piece. With the WP-100, it was very easy to push the handle all the way down the hook, either by accident or just because of its design, stressing the hook and eventually breaking it; there was nothing to stop the handle to slide all the way down. As said, mine broke. That was a poor design, fixed on the Aquarius; now you just put the handle on the holder, it cannot be pushed all the way down. Some have argued that makes it difficult to handle the hose, but I didn&#x27;t find any issues, the hose juts hang there by simple gravity, it doesn&#x27;t tangle or interfere with the unit in any way&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;-The reservoir valve was replaced by a metal spring mechanism. This was a another design flaw of the WP-100, its reservoir valve consist of a rubber piece, very cheap in my opinion, which eventually gives up and start leaking after a few years. As said before, the only way to fix it is by buying an entire new reservoir as the little rubber piece is not available alone, which means not only paying way more but also a waste of resources. In contrast, the WP-660 has a stainless steel spring with a plastic cap, that appears way more durable and also a much better and higher quality solution. Only time will tell but it seems it will last longer than the one in the WP-100&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;-The knob to graduate the pressure is easier to operate. The WP-100 has a hole to put both fingers in, on the Aquarius is a protruding knob, very easy to reach and to manipulate, way better I think, easier to find when in use if needed. And also more ergonomic&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;-The Aquarius handle has an on-off switch that actually works. The WP-100 has that dreadful push button on the handle that you need to press constantly to stop the flow of water, doesn&#x27;t stop it completely and also causes the Waterpik to make a noise like the pump is being damaged while the pressure is reverted. Not good at all, it was a poor solution at best, a useless feature at worst, it just didn&#x27;t work. On the WP-660, there is an actual on-off button; in fact the correct way to operate this new Waterpik is to turn it on the base first, then turn it on via the handle when you already have the tip inside your mouth ready to go, the water doesn&#x27;t come out unless you turn the handle on. This is much better than having to reach the switch on the base unit with the tip in your mouth or having to hold into the appalling pressure cutting button on the handle and then release it. All this while water was still coming out of the tip as the button didn&#x27;t cut the water flow completely.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;-The pace timer.  This feature is non-existent on the Ultra, and I realized it is very helpful. I use the Waterpik first on the upper section of the mouth, outside-inside and then move to the lower section, in-out and I&#x27;m done. At a pressure level of 8, the water in the reservoir, at full capacity, should last little less than 90 seconds.  The Aquarius will give you a very short flow pause at 30 seconds of use and another at 60 seconds, this is good to pace your cleaning as it should take about 30 seconds to clean each part of the mouth, up and down, and then you have an extra 20 seconds to touch-up. This avoids you having to be periodically peaking over to the reservoir to see how much water is left and instead allow you to concentrate on the cleaning and doing the job properly&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;-The reservoir cover is now part of the unit. If you are like my mother in law that misplaces everything - sorry mom, I still love you-, chances are you have misplaced the reservoir cover of the WP-100 (as my mother in law did). This cover also contains the tips so it can be kind of an inconvenience to lose it. On the WP-660, the cover is attached with a hinge mechanism to the body of the Waterpik, no way to lose it. The tips are now stored on the unit itself, behind the reservoir&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The rest is about the same as the WP-100, it comes with a bunch of tips from which you will probably only use the classic jet, and a 3 years warranty. It also includes a gum massaging mode which is pointless as you can achieve the same results by regulating the pressure knob. One disadvantage to the WP-100 is that you can only store two tips on the unit and not four, but again if you are like me that use only one, this is not an issue. But it might be for some users, if you have braces for example or like to regularly use the one designed for root canal maintenance (the Pik Pocket). One thing that was bad on the WP-100 and remain as bad on the WP-660 is cable management, there is no place to wrap the cable or at least a Velcro band included to deal with the cable, this lack of cablemanagement is in part responsible for the damage to my WP-100 power cord, the cord is just hanging there. A needed improvement for the next design, please take note Waterpik&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Overall, I see no disadvantages when compared with the WP-100 and instead see many advantages. Until the unit has more years in the market, speculating about its durability without real facts is pointless at this time, so far the Aquarius works the same or better than the Ultra so it&#x27;s higher price is justifiable. And you can even get a good deal and get it at the same price or a little cheaper than the Ultra, which is a real bargainul. I use the Waterpik first on the upper section of the mouth, outside-inside and then move to the lower section, in-out and I&#x27;m done. At a pressure level of 8, the water in the reservoir, at full capacity, should last little less than 90 seconds.  The Aquarius will give you a very short flow pause at 30 seconds of use and another at 60 seconds, this is good to pace your cleaning as it should take about 30 seconds to clean each part of the mouth, up and down, and then you have an extra 20 seconds to touch-up.     <li> I love this water flosser. It is small and compact to fit nicely in my small bathroom. I call it my teeth and gum tool.
